Post: <a href="#p490724653" class="quotelink">&gt;&gt;490724653</a><br>Youre a retard, OP. This is completely computationally unfeasible. The computational complexity of most decision and inference problems on a network grows extremely rapidly as a function of the total number of nodes and edges. The computational complexity of most of these problems is going to grow exponentially as a function of the number of edges. Most of these problems would be impossible to solve even on a network with a few dozen nodes. A network of all financial transactions would have billions of nodes. A complete graph with just 100 nodes has k=100*99/2=4950 edges. A computational problem in the complexity class O(2^k) on such a network will then involve on the order of 2^4950 computations for a network with just 100 nodes. This exceeds the number of particles in the observable universe, which is on the order of 4x10^80. The value 2^4950 is much, much larger. Moreover, since this is a real-world network, the topology will actually be changing constantly over time, with new nodes and links forming, and old ones disappearing. Under these sort of conditions, you&#039;re not even going to be able to completely track and predict the behavior of more than a few dozen nodes at a time.
